From pm at nellump.ath.cx  Thu Aug 11 21:15:39 2005
From: pm at nellump.ath.cx (Paul Mullen)
Date: Thu, 11 Aug 2005 21:15:39 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] CD Ripping Apps  WAS: ipods
In-Reply-To: <42FB8201.21992.243D1D96@localhost>
References: <20050811071626.GA22556@nellump.ath.cx>
	<42FB8201.21992.243D1D96@localhost>
Message-ID: <20050812041539.GC29566@nellump.ath.cx>

On Thu, Aug 11, 2005 at 04:51:13PM -0700, John Jordan wrote:
> 
> Then I tried to use it. I typed "abcde" and it started ripping the
> CD that was in the drive. There were no questions beforehand. I
> suppose there are some switches for options, but I didn't know what
> they were.

Did you RTFM? "man abcde" presents a fairly readable user's guide.

I'm not sure why it neither queried CDDB nor offered you any options
before ripping. Perhaps your distribution has different defaults than
mine. As far as I can tell, you have to explicitly tell it to not
query CDDB.

Create a ".abcde.conf" file in your home directory and paste in the
following:

   OUTPUTTYPE="mp3"
   
   LAMEOPTS="--vbr-new -B 320"
   
   OUTPUTFORMAT='${ARTISTFILE}/${ALBUMFILE}/${TRACKNUM}-${TRACKFILE}'
   VAOUTPUTFORMAT='Compilations/${ALBUMFILE}/${TRACKNUM}-${ARTISTFILE}-${TRACKFILE}'
   PADTRACKS=y
   
   CDDBLOCALDIR=~/.cddb
   CDDBCOPYLOCAL=y
   CDDBUSELOCAL=y
   EJECTCD=y

That'll have it create VBR-encoded MP3s at 320 kbps (and includes a
few other preferred settings).

> I ripped this previously with Grip (couldn't get it to rip four of
> the nine tracks as one file), with k3b (lousy quality), and with
> both I had to type in by hand the name of the piece, the artist, and
> the filename. Not sure if abcde is really designed for this sort of
> ripping task.

I'm unaware of any app that will complete the ripping process with the
end result being one giant file. It's certainly possible to do this
"by hand", though. You'll need a ripper (like "cdparanoia"), and an
encoder (like "lame"), but if you've already installed a shiny GUI app
chances are it relies on these very programs and has already installed
them.

1) Determine how many tracks on are the CD:

   cdparanoia -Q

2) Rip the entire audio CD to one giant file (example assumes a disc
with 10 tracks):

   cdparanoia 1-10

3) Encode to MP3 (320 kbps VBR file):

   lame --vbr-new -B 320 cdda.wav happy_fun_file.mp3

It worked on my box, at least.


Paul

From nsxfreddy at gmail.com  Fri Aug 12 18:26:56 2005
From: nsxfreddy at gmail.com (Jason R. Martin)
Date: Fri, 12 Aug 2005 18:26:56 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] rpmbuild equivlent to make --prefix
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0508121715001.5591-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.33.0508121715001.5591-100000@main.cyber-office.net>
Message-ID: <c29537840508121826364f982d@mail.gmail.com>

On 8/12/05, Roderick A. Anderson <raanders at acm.org> wrote:
> I'm trying to build an RPM and can't figure out how to pass/get a
> --prefix=/etc to the make process.
> 
> The documention for the package gives either the ./configure, make, make
> install or the rpmbuild -bb instructions but the non-rpmbuild is the only
> one that discusses how to change the from the default /usr/local/etc to
> /etc.
> 
> It is a pretty abreviated spec file and prefix never shows up in it.
> There is a _configuredir but it is never set anywhere that I can find.
> 
> Once again I've had a long day and am short on brain power.

>From Maximum RPM[1]:

"The prefix tag is used when a relocatable package is to be built. A relocatable
package can be installed normally or can be installed in a
user-specified directory, by
using RPM's --prefix install-time option. The data specified after the prefix
tag should be the part of the package's path that may be changed
during installation.
For example, if the following prefix line was included in a spec file:

Prefix: /opt

and the following file was specified in the spec file's %files list:

/opt/blather/foonly

then the file foonly would be installed in /opt/blather if the package was
installed normally. It would be installed in /usr/local/blather if the package
was installed with the --prefix /usr/local option."

So, in summary, try adding a Prefix: /blah to the spec file that
matches the prefix of the files in the %files list, then you should be
able to install the package with rpm -ivh --prefix=/ blah.rpm.

Jason

[1] http://www.redhat.com/docs/books/max-rpm/index.html

Paul,

Thanks for that additional information. I've got it working now. It's 
not perfect, but I can handle the imperfect parts.

First imperfect part is that lame can't handle spaces in the output 
mp3 file. Not a biggie, I just use Nautilus to rename it before adding 
it to the list in gtkpod. It also doesn't get the CDDB information, but 
I can add that with gtkpod from the disk label. Frankly, when I used 
apps that automatically queried the CDDB database online, half the 
time the data was screwed up anyway.

Another weirditude is that cdparanoia runs the CPU at 800 on my 
computer, but when I encode, lame runs it at 2G. As a result it's 
kinda slow on the ripping. A 40-minute symphony encodes in about 
2 minutes, though.

I do have another question unrelated to the rip/encode process. A 
couple times the iPod has suddenly become unmounted. 
Unplugging it and plugging it back in does not remount it. I tried 
mount /media/iPod, but it just said the device didn't exist. It was 
like the USB port was not working. Except that it was, because I 
use a USB mouse, and it never stopped working. Eventually I shut 
down and restarted the computer. That did it. Afterwards it 
mounted automatically when plugged in, as before. And since the 
iPod was unchanged, the problem must have been in the 
computer, not in the iPod.

Shutting down and restarting is a PITA. Is there a "modprobe 
hotplug system" command that I can use to reset the USB ports 
for the next time this happens?

Thanks for the advice about abcde. You may end up converting me 
to a command-line guy. OK, that may take a while. :)


From johnxj at comcast.net  Sat Aug 13 12:08:58 2005
From: johnxj at comcast.net (John Jordan)
Date: Sat, 13 Aug 2005 12:08:58 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] ipods
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0508111740100.9157@shaft.bitmine.net>
References: <42FB7F8E.15885.24338C10@localhost>
Message-ID: <42FDE2DA.19554.2D876D3E@localhost>

On 11 Aug 2005, at 18:14, Jeme A Brelin wrote:

> > Eventually I got it to rip, but it still insisted on ripping each
> > track as a separate "song." I needed to get it to rip each track as
> > part of one larger file for the whole symphony. In addition, I
> > needed to add a couple seconds quiet space in between each track. I
> > never figured out how to do that or how to get it to make several
> > tracks into one file.
> 
> I don't know of anything out there that's going to do what you want.
> Everything I know that rips CDs rips them track by track.  You can,
> however, join the files when you're done.  You can even keep a couple
> of seconds of blank audio in a file and insert that between tracks
> (there may be a more elegant way of doing this, but I've spent no time
> thinking about it).
> 
> Quite frankly, however, I'm not sure why you'd do this.  The tracks
> are there to help you navigate the piece.  You lose nothing by keeping
> them except when you use "Shuffle" mode, but nobody does that with
> symphonic music anyway.  If you keep the tracks separate and make sure
> they have appropriate track numbers in their ID3 tags, you can listen
> to them in sequence (with appropriate between-track pauses) whenever
> you like.

OK, let me explain what I want to do.

Suppose you just got home from shopping at Classical Millennium, 
as I did the other day. I scored a used copy of Beethoven's 9th, the 
awesome version by Bernstein in Berlin right after the wall came 
down. Bernstein, Jewish, gay, parents holocaust escapees to 
America, conducting in Berlin the most impressive piece of music 
Germany ever produced -- and at the end they changed Ode to Joy 
to Ode to Freedom. It was broadcast live, and at the end people 
were pouring out onto the streets bawling.

Now, the first thing I did was pop this into the stereo and sit back 
to listen to it. Note that I did not wish to play just one track. I 
wanted to listen to the whole thing all at once. I will never want to 
listen to just one track of this CD. Or of any other symphony. So if 
I rip one track at a time, then I have to create a zillion playlists, one 
for each symphonic work. It's much easier to have all the tracks as 
one file. I want my iPod to work just like my stereo -- pop in a CD 
and listen to the whole thing.

But having said that, sometimes I might not want to rip the whole 
CD as one file. Lots of times the publisher will put several works on 
one CD. For example, I am currently ripping a CD that has 
Beethoven's 1st, 7th and Leonore #3 -- nine tracks. If I rip this as 
three files, it will work even better than the stereo, because each 
file will be one complete work.

> > I also never figured out how to name the file and the tracks so they
> > would show up correctly on the iPod.
> 
> Naming them doesn't do diddly.  You need to modify their ID3 tags.  I
> use a combination of the id3v2 and mp3info utilities.  While the
> latter doesn't support version 2 tags, the former has crappy syntax
> and can be a pain to put into scripts.  Essentially, I use id3v2 for
> writing tags and mp3info for reading them in little shell scripts that
> I write to manipulate these things.

I finally figured out how to do that with gtkpod. Stupidly simple, 
really. Just click twice on the name and it switches the name to 
edit mode -- just like a file in Nautilus or Windows Explorer. Dunno 
why I was so dense not to figure that out. (I was right-clicking on it, 
which does not list a "rename" option.)

> > After hours and hours of reading about it, perusing the help,
> > scouring the internet, and asking users on web pages and blogs, I
> > just gave up on it.
> 
> It's really no big deal.  What exactly is your problem?

I found something that works better than Grip -- abcde with the 
advice from Paul Mullen. See other post.

> > Not sure I really want iTunes on my Linux computer.
> 
> I wouldn't touch it with a ten meter cattle prod.

On that we totally agree.

> computer, but when I encode, lame runs it at 2G. As a result it's 
> kinda slow on the ripping. A 40-minute symphony encodes in about 
> 2 minutes, though.

I would guess ripping stuff from the CD isn't CPU-bound, but rather I/O
bound by the CD-ROM drive itself.  In such cases, it wouldn't matter if
your CPU were running at 7.1GHz... it would still rip at the same old speed.

Encoding, on the other hand, is CPU-bound most of the time.... so the
extra CPU horsepower helps speed things up significantly.  :-)

As for spaces in filenames, did you try manually escaping the spaces?

A file named:
Big and Rich - Wild West Show.mp3

Would be typed as:
Big\ and\ Rich\ -\ Wild\ West\ Show.mp3

...note the spaces being escaped with backslashes.

Rob

From jeme at brelin.net  Sat Aug 13 14:15:27 2005
From: jeme at brelin.net (Jeme A Brelin)
Date: Sat, 13 Aug 2005 14:15:27 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] ipods
In-Reply-To: <42FDE2DA.19554.2D876D3E@localhost>

On Sat, 13 Aug 2005, John Jordan wrote:
> I will never want to listen to just one track of this CD. Or of any 
> other symphony.

Yeah, that's fine.  But just because you don't think right now that you're 
ever going to want to listen to just one track you don't have to give up 
the navigability of the track breaks (which are useful for, say, 
illustrating your point to a friend about the way the strings come in 
during the second movement or what have you).

> So if I rip one track at a time, then I have to create a zillion 
> playlists, one for each symphonic work.

See, that's where you're mistaken.  You don't have to do that.  That 
really would be absurd.

The same is true for pop albums or whatever.  You don't have to create a 
playlist for each album and you can still listen to the tracks in the 
order the publisher intended.

> It's much easier to have all the tracks as one file.

No easier, just less flexible.

> I want my iPod to work just like my stereo -- pop in a CD and listen to 
> the whole thing.

It already does.  If you browse your collection by "album" (which doesn't 
exactly apply in this case, but I'll explain how to make it work that 
way), when you select and play the first track of the album, the rest of 
the album will follow in sequence.

Use your ID3 tags!  Here's how I do my symphonic music using only ID3v1 
tags (since the v2 tags that are most useful for symphonic music are not 
read by the iPod).

Let's say I've got the following directory (and I do):

jbrelin at person:~$ ls /usr/local/public/mp3/ipod/Henryk_Gorecki/Symphony_No_3/
Lento_E_Largo__Tranquillissimo.mp3
Lento__Cantabile__Semplice.mp3
Lento__Sostenuto_Tranquillo_Ma_Cantabile.mp3

Then the tracks in this directory have the following ID3 tags:

Title:   Lento - Sostenuto Tranquillo Ma Cantabile
Artist:  Henryk Gorecki
Album:   Symphony No 3
Track: 1
Year:  1976

Title:   Lento E Largo - Tranquillissimo
Artist:  Henryk Gorecki
Album:   Symphony No 3
Track: 2
Year:  1976

Title:   Lento - Cantabile - Semplice
Artist:  Henryk Gorecki
Album:   Symphony No 3
Track: 3
Year:  1976

Note that the filenames are just the titles of the movements.  Doesn't 
matter that they're not alphabetical or anything.  I don't intend to have 
different versions of this particular work ever (this is the one from 1992 
with Dawn Upshaw doing the aria -- amazing), so I didn't bother with a 
special notation in the album or artist field to distinguish it from 
others.

You, however, might do things a little differently.  You might use the 
ID3V2 Composer tag and the regular Artist tag for conductor, for example. 
Your iPod will only list the conductor in that case unless you modify the 
album title.

I'm more inclined to use a scheme where I list some identifying 
information about the piece in the Album field.  For this one, if I ever 
had to deal with a conflict, I might list it as follows:

Album: Symphony No. 3 - London Sinfonietta - 1992

Then when I chose that album on my iPod and played the first listed track 
(which would be the first in the symphony regardless of how the files are 
named), it will play the whole thing straight through.

> But having said that, sometimes I might not want to rip the whole CD as 
> one file. Lots of times the publisher will put several works on one CD. 
> For example, I am currently ripping a CD that has Beethoven's 1st, 7th 
> and Leonore #3 -- nine tracks. If I rip this as three files, it will 
> work even better than the stereo, because each file will be one complete 
> work.


Rip the tracks, adjust the tags.  Way less work, more flexibile, lose 
nothing.

I do this and I just keep ONE playlist of all my pop songs (including 
country, rock, whatever -- just modern "songs") and use that for shuffle 
mode when I'm out and about.  I can generate this playlist with a script 
that adds everything that doesn't have the genre tag set to one of the 
following:

32: Classical
101: Speech
102: Chanson
103: Opera
104: Chamber Music
105: Sonata
106: Symphony

> I finally figured out how to do that with gtkpod. Stupidly simple, 
> really. Just click twice on the name and it switches the name to edit 
> mode -- just like a file in Nautilus or Windows Explorer. Dunno why I 
> was so dense not to figure that out. (I was right-clicking on it, which 
> does not list a "rename" option.)

Right, in gtkpod, you're not renaming the files, you're editting the ID3 
tags.  I find this is easier to do en mass from the command line with 
id3v2.

> I found something that works better than Grip -- abcde with the advice 
> from Paul Mullen. See other post.

Curious to see why you think it works better than grip.  The functionality 
is identical, but grip gives you a better interface for randomly modifying 
track names before the rip.

abcde works great in the way that Sean is using it (on a headless ripping 
machine), but when you're working on a desktop, the interface is not 
particularly flexible.

J.

From ckonstan at lunarlogic.com  Sat Aug 13 17:05:08 2005
From: ckonstan at lunarlogic.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Sat, 13 Aug 2005 17:05:08 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] FW: Can't bootup linux
In-Reply-To: <NAEMLOHDCGGNKGMHCPFGMECMCDAA.jimwebb@charter.net>
References: <NAEMLOHDCGGNKGMHCPFGMECMCDAA.jimwebb@charter.net>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0508131640000.6416@localhost>

Use fdisk -l to see where your partitions are.  Do you have /boot
mounted on its own partition?  You'll have to mount it:

cd /boot
ls -l

If you see 0 entries listed, try this:

cd /
mount /dev/hda1 /boot   # This assumes /dev/hda1 is your /boot partition
cd /boot
ls -l

You should see files now.

On redhat, /boot/grub/grub.conf should be the location of the file.

>From a grub prompt at bootup time, you can manually type in any commands
that one would find in a grub.conf file.  You can try out various
vmlinuz lines from there, without having to get all the way to a place
where you can edit the grub.conf file.  You can get to the prompt by
typing "c" when yu see the grub menu screen.  Try this out for fun at
the grub prompt:

root (hd0,0) # Use the right numbers, of course.  These point to the first
              # partition on the first drive, a good place to put your
              # /boot partition.  It is the equivalent of /dev/hda1.

configfile /grub/grub.conf # This assumes /boot is its own partition.
                            # If /boot is part of your root filesystem,
                            # use the path /boot/grub/grub.conf instead.

These 2 commands at the grub prompt will manually launch the grub menu.
You can also type in commands like the following to boot "manually":

root (hd0,0)
kernel /vmlinuz-2.6.12-gentoo-r4 root=/dev/hda5 ro lang=en vga=791
boot

This is straight out of my menu.lst file (the debian and gentoo name for
grub.conf).  The grub.conf file's entries get executed as-is when you
choose one at bootup time, as if you typed them yourself at the prompt.
As you can see, my root filesystem is on /dev/hda5, the first extended
partition of the disk.  You alluded to a syntax that lets grub figure
out the root filesystem partition for itself (root=LABEL=/).  I suggest
spelling it out explicitly as I have done here.

Do you need an initrd image?  If it's a stock redhat kernel, I would say
it's a certainty.  I have not used an initrd image for a long time, so I
have no known working example to offer you.  But it's not too hard; it
looks like the "kernel" line, except with no params.  Here's a googled
one:

initrd /initrd-2.4.18-0.12.img

You would put this somewhere between the "root" line and the "boot" line.
Again, you can see that "/boot" is not part of the path.  This is
because /boot is its own partition on this machine.  If /boot were part
of the root filesystem, all the paths in grub.conf would have "/boot"
prepended.

With a stock redhat kernel, your kernel will be unable to read your hard
drive without the assistance of the modules in that initrd image.  I'd
bet that is your problem.  No ATA support, no workie.  Add an initrd
line to your grub commands in grub.conf, or type the lines in manually
from the grub prompt.

Carlos

From jeme at brelin.net  Sat Aug 13 17:22:35 2005

On Sat, 13 Aug 2005, John Jordan wrote:
> First imperfect part is that lame can't handle spaces in the output mp3 
> file. Not a biggie, I just use Nautilus to rename it before adding it to 
> the list in gtkpod.

You can put the filename in quotes and the spaces will be interpreted 
literally as part of one string.  Also, you can escape the quotes as 
follows:

filename\ with\ spaces.mp3

That should be equivalent to "filename with spaces.mp3" to your shell.

> It also doesn't get the CDDB information, but I can add that with gtkpod 
> from the disk label.

Um, pain in the butt.

> Frankly, when I used apps that automatically queried the CDDB database 
> online, half the time the data was screwed up anyway.

If you use grip, you can hit the little pencil button and then edit the 
CDDB information that it queried.  Furthermore, you can resubmit your 
changes so that the rest of us get proper information next time.  It's a 
simple way to give something back.

> Another weirditude is that cdparanoia runs the CPU at 800 on my 
> computer, but when I encode, lame runs it at 2G. As a result it's kinda 
> slow on the ripping.

It depends on how much "paranoia" cdparanoia is using.  There are 
command-line options to modify how this is done.  In grip, there are check 
boxes to disable various levels of paranoia to speed up the process. 
(Disabling paranoia can make the rip less fault tolerant, of course.)

> I do have another question unrelated to the rip/encode process. A couple 
> times the iPod has suddenly become unmounted. Unplugging it and plugging 
> it back in does not remount it. I tried mount /media/iPod, but it just 
> said the device didn't exist. It was like the USB port was not working.

You're doing this via USB?  Weird.  Is it USB 2.0?  I use firewire.

> Eventually I shut down and restarted the computer. That did it.

You need the rescan-scsi-bus.sh script.

When it gets flakey, you have to rescan the bus and verify the devices. 
Obviously, rebooting the machine will rescan the bus.

> Shutting down and restarting is a PITA. Is there a "modprobe hotplug 
> system" command that I can use to reset the USB ports for the next time 
> this happens?

Heh.  I should read the whole thing before replying to pieces.

> Thanks for the advice about abcde. You may end up converting me to a 
> command-line guy. OK, that may take a while. :)

You'll certainly find that using the command-line is easier for bulk 
renaming and modifying ID3 tags in your MP3s.  But these are processes you 
want to automate for the most part, so scripting makes sense.  For 
ripping, I don't see the advantage (and I'm a VERY command-line kind of 
guy).

J.

From jeme at brelin.net  Sat Aug 13 17:33:34 2005
From: jeme at brelin.net (Jeme A Brelin)
Date: Sat, 13 Aug 2005 17:33:34 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] CD Ripping Apps  WAS: ipods
In-Reply-To: <42FDE9B5.28051.2DA233FB@localhost>
References: <42FDE2C8.6358.2D8724FA@localhost>
	<42FDE9B5.28051.2DA233FB@localhost>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0508131723140.31915@shaft.bitmine.net>


On Sat, 13 Aug 2005, John Jordan wrote:
> Now that you point that out, I watched the drive light while it was 
> ripping and it was on continuously. While encoding it flickered on and 
> off, but was off more than on. So your theory makes sense.

Uh, huh?  The cdrom light was on when you were encoding and NOT ripping?

The CDROM drive shouldn't be accessed at all when you're just encoding (no 
lights).  If you're ripping, the light should be more or less constantly 
engaged... even if you're encoding simultaneously.

> I'm just happy that I'm finally able to rip and encode the way I want 
> to. :)

But are you?

>> A file named:
>> Big and Rich - Wild West Show.mp3
>>
>> Would be typed as:
>> Big\ and\ Rich\ -\ Wild\ West\ Show.mp3
>>
>> ...note the spaces being escaped with backslashes.
>
> Good tip! I didn't know that! I tried it and it works! It's also better 
> than renaming in flaky Nautilus, because some of the "rename" buttons in 
> Nautilus don't work.

Quotes use fewer keystrokes and are less likely to cause weird errors 
(like when you forget to escape one of your spaces and it's read as two 
arguments).  It also does wonders for readability.

Consider the following:

id3v2 -t "The Space Between Us (Turns Into Animals)" "Robyn Hitchock & 
The Egyptians - The Space Between Us (Turns Into Animals).mp3"

versus

id3v2 -t The\ Space\ Between\ Us\ \(Turns\ Into Animals\) Robyn\ Hitchock\ 
\&\ The\ Egyptians\ -\ The\ Space\ Between\ Us\ \(Turns\ Into\ 
Animals\).mp3

Which is more readable?  Which is easier to read and distinguish when one 
argument ends and another begins?

Did you notice there's an error in the second one and there is no escape 
on the space before the word "Animals" in the title tag?  I didn't until 
just now.

Ugly.

Personally, I use underscores instead of spaces anyway because I write 
lots of shell scripts and don't want to have to worry about quoting my 
variables all the time.  I also keep directories by artist and album 
subdirectories, then store track information in the ID3 tags.  As a 
result, the above file would be here (for instance):

/usr/local/mp3/ipod/Robyn_Hitchcock_And_The_Egyptians/Globe_Of_Frogs/The_Shapes_Between_Us_Turn_Into_Animals.mp3

J.

      Jeme A Brelin
     jeme at brelin.net

     /dev/hda4                                                 f    Win95
Ext'd (LBA)
     /dev/hda5                                                 83   Linux
     /dev/hda6                                                 83   Linux
     /dev/hda7                                                 82 Linux swap

>

> mount /dev/hda1 /boot   # This assumes /dev/hda1 is your /boot partition

I tried this and got mount: Mounting /dev/hda/1 on /boot failed: No such
file or directory
Does RH have /boot directory??????  I have typed find boot with the message
of no such file or directory

>cd /boot
> ls -l
>
> You should see files now.
>
> On redhat, /boot/grub/grub.conf should be the location of the file.
>
> >From a grub prompt at bootup time, you can manually type in any commands
> that one would find in a grub.conf file.  You can try out various
> vmlinuz lines from there, without having to get all the way to a place
> where you can edit the grub.conf file.  You can get to the prompt by
> typing "c" when yu see the grub menu screen.  Try this out for fun at
> the grub prompt:
>
> root (hd0,0) # Use the right numbers, of course.  These point to the first
>               # partition on the first drive, a good place to put your
>               # /boot partition.  It is the equivalent of /dev/hda1.
>
> configfile /grub/grub.conf # This assumes /boot is its own partition.
>                             # If /boot is part of your root filesystem,
>                             # use the path /boot/grub/grub.conf instead.
>
> These 2 commands at the grub prompt will manually launch the grub menu.
> You can also type in commands like the following to boot "manually":
>
> root (hd0,0)
> kernel /vmlinuz-2.6.12-gentoo-r4 root=/dev/hda5 ro lang=en vga=791
> boot
>
> This is straight out of my menu.lst file (the debian and gentoo name for
> grub.conf).  The grub.conf file's entries get executed as-is when you
> choose one at bootup time, as if you typed them yourself at the prompt.
> As you can see, my root filesystem is on /dev/hda5, the first extended
> partition of the disk.  You alluded to a syntax that lets grub figure
> out the root filesystem partition for itself (root=LABEL=/).  I suggest
> spelling it out explicitly as I have done here.
>
> Do you need an initrd image?  If it's a stock redhat kernel, I would say
> it's a certainty.  I have not used an initrd image for a long time, so I
> have no known working example to offer you.  But it's not too hard; it
> looks like the "kernel" line, except with no params.  Here's a googled
> one:
>
> initrd /initrd-2.4.18-0.12.img
>
> You would put this somewhere between the "root" line and the "boot" line.
> Again, you can see that "/boot" is not part of the path.  This is
> because /boot is its own partition on this machine.  If /boot were part
> of the root filesystem, all the paths in grub.conf would have "/boot"
> prepended.
>
> With a stock redhat kernel, your kernel will be unable to read your hard
> drive without the assistance of the modules in that initrd image.  I'd
> bet that is your problem.  No ATA support, no workie.  Add an initrd
> line to your grub commands in grub.conf, or type the lines in manually
> from the grub prompt.
>
> Carlos
>

From ckonstan at lunarlogic.com  Sat Aug 13 17:46:53 2005
From: ckonstan at lunarlogic.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Sat, 13 Aug 2005 17:46:53 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] FW: Can't bootup linux
In-Reply-To: <NAEMLOHDCGGNKGMHCPFGOECNCDAA.jimwebb@charter.net>
References: <NAEMLOHDCGGNKGMHCPFGOECNCDAA.jimwebb@charter.net>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0508131739120.6416@localhost>

The redhat 8 installer program puts you into a GUI fdisk utility.  You
set up the partitions yourself.  There may be an "automatic" option, and
I have no idea what that does exactly.  Judging by the mess of
partitions you have, I'd say you chose this option at install time.

Your fdisk output below does not give Start, End and Blocks for all
entries.  This would be crucial info in deciding which partition is
/boot.  /boot will be a very small partition, usually no more than 100
megabytes.  It will be type 83 (Linux), not 82 (Linux Swap) or f
(Win95).

Why is /dev/hda3 listed twice?  Is something screwy with your hard drive
or MBR?

Since dev/hda1 is marked as the active partition, one would think that
is the /boot partition.  Try mounting it again, and see to it that you
have no typos this time (you typed /dev/hda/1 last time instead of
/dev/hda1).

Carlos

From ckonstan at lunarlogic.com  Sat Aug 13 18:03:39 2005
From: ckonstan at lunarlogic.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Sat, 13 Aug 2005 18:03:39 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] FW: Can't bootup linux
In-Reply-To: <NAEMLOHDCGGNKGMHCPFGIECOCDAA.jimwebb@charter.net>
References: <NAEMLOHDCGGNKGMHCPFGIECOCDAA.jimwebb@charter.net>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0508131753230.6416@localhost>

This looks plain broken:

kernel /vmlinuz-2.4.18-18.8.0 ro root=LABEL=/ hda =ide-scsi

The "root=LABEL=/", "hda" and "=ide-scsi" are broken by whitespace that
would appear to render this line syntactically incorrect.

Try this instead:

kernel /vmlinuz-2.4.18-18.8.0 ro root=/dev/hda5

This assumes your root filesystem is on /dev/hda5.

Once you get this to work, you can add back in the scsi support for your
CDROM.  You need to find out which device your CDROM is, of course.
Try either dmesg|less or:

eject /dev/hdb
eject /dev/hdc
eject /dev/hdd

See which one opens your CDROM tray (not sure if eject will work without
scsi support - you may have to read the dmesg output instead).  Once you
find it, modify the kernel line to look like this:

kernel /vmlinuz-2.4.18-18.8.0 ro root=/dev/hda5 /dev/hdc=ide-scsi

This assumes your CDROM is /dev/hdc (which will be the case if it's the
master device on the second IDE cable).

Carlos

>> As you can see, my root filesystem is on /dev/hda5, the first extended
>> partition of the disk.  You alluded to a syntax that lets grub figure
>> out the root filesystem partition for itself (root=LABEL=/).  I suggest
>> spelling it out explicitly as I have done here.
>>
>> Do you need an initrd image?  If it's a stock redhat kernel, I would say
>> it's a certainty.  I have not used an initrd image for a long time, so I
>> have no known working example to offer you.  But it's not too hard; it
>> looks like the "kernel" line, except with no params.  Here's a googled
>> one:
>>
>> initrd /initrd-2.4.18-0.12.img
>>
>> You would put this somewhere between the "root" line and the "boot" line.
>> Again, you can see that "/boot" is not part of the path.  This is
>> because /boot is its own partition on this machine.  If /boot were part
>> of the root filesystem, all the paths in grub.conf would have "/boot"
>> prepended.
>>
>> With a stock redhat kernel, your kernel will be unable to read your hard
>> drive without the assistance of the modules in that initrd image.  I'd
>> bet that is your problem.  No ATA support, no workie.  Add an initrd
>> line to your grub commands in grub.conf, or type the lines in manually
>> from the grub prompt.
>>
>> Carlos
>>

> to the first
> >>               # partition on the first drive, a good place to put your

Carlos,

Edited root=/dev/hda* using 1-7 since that is what fdisk -l shows as dev.  I
get the following on all of them:

Mounting root filesystem
attempt to access beyond end of device
03:04: rw=0, want=2, limit=1
EXT3-fs: unable to read superblock
mount: error 22 mounting ext3
pivotroot: pivot_root(/sysroot,/sysroot/initrd) failed: 2
umount /initrd/proc failed: 2
Freeing unused kernel memory: 172k freed
Kernel panic: No init found.  Try passing init= option to kernel.


> -----Original Message-----
> From: plug-bounces at lists.pdxlinux.org
> [mailto:plug-bounces at lists.pdxlinux.org]On Behalf Of Carlos Konstanski
> Sent: Saturday, August 13, 2005 9:04 PM
> To: General Linux/UNIX discussion and help;civil and on-topic
> Subject: RE: [PLUG] FW: Can't bootup linux
>
>
> This looks plain broken:
>
> kernel /vmlinuz-2.4.18-18.8.0 ro root=LABEL=/ hda =ide-scsi
>
> The "root=LABEL=/", "hda" and "=ide-scsi" are broken by whitespace that
> would appear to render this line syntactically incorrect.
>
> Try this instead:
>
> kernel /vmlinuz-2.4.18-18.8.0 ro root=/dev/hda5
>
> This assumes your root filesystem is on /dev/hda5.
>
> Once you get this to work, you can add back in the scsi support for your
> CDROM.  You need to find out which device your CDROM is, of course.
> Try either dmesg|less or:
>
> eject /dev/hdb
> eject /dev/hdc
> eject /dev/hdd
>
> See which one opens your CDROM tray (not sure if eject will work without
> scsi support - you may have to read the dmesg output instead).  Once you
> find it, modify the kernel line to look like this:
>
> kernel /vmlinuz-2.4.18-18.8.0 ro root=/dev/hda5 /dev/hdc=ide-scsi
>
> This assumes your CDROM is /dev/hdc (which will be the case if it's the
> master device on the second IDE cable).
>
> Carlos
>

> -----Original Message-----
> From: plug-bounces at lists.pdxlinux.org
> [mailto:plug-bounces at lists.pdxlinux.org]On Behalf Of Carlos Konstanski
> Sent: Saturday, August 13, 2005 9:04 PM
> To: General Linux/UNIX discussion and help;civil and on-topic
> Subject: RE: [PLUG] FW: Can't bootup linux
>
>
> This looks plain broken:
>
> kernel /vmlinuz-2.4.18-18.8.0 ro root=LABEL=/ hda =ide-scsi
>
> The "root=LABEL=/", "hda" and "=ide-scsi" are broken by whitespace that
> would appear to render this line syntactically incorrect.
>
> Try this instead:
>
> kernel /vmlinuz-2.4.18-18.8.0 ro root=/dev/hda5
>
> This assumes your root filesystem is on /dev/hda5.
>
> Once you get this to work, you can add back in the scsi support for your
> CDROM.  You need to find out which device your CDROM is, of course.
> Try either dmesg|less or:
>
> eject /dev/hdb
> eject /dev/hdc
> eject /dev/hdd
>
> See which one opens your CDROM tray (not sure if eject will work without
> scsi support - you may have to read the dmesg output instead).  Once you
> find it, modify the kernel line to look like this:
>
> kernel /vmlinuz-2.4.18-18.8.0 ro root=/dev/hda5 /dev/hdc=ide-scsi
>
> This assumes your CDROM is /dev/hdc (which will be the case if it's the
> master device on the second IDE cable).
>
> Carlos
>
> On Sat, 13 Aug 2005, James H. Webb wrote:

> >
> >> root (hd0,0) # Use the right numbers, of course.  These point
> to the first
> >>               # partition on the first drive, a good place to put your
> >>               # /boot partition.  It is the equivalent of /dev/hda1.
> >>
> >> configfile /grub/grub.conf # This assumes /boot is its own partition.
> >>                             # If /boot is part of your root filesystem,
> >>                             # use the path
> /boot/grub/grub.conf instead.
> >>
> >> These 2 commands at the grub prompt will manually launch the grub menu.
> >> You can also type in commands like the following to boot "manually":
> >>
> >> root (hd0,0)
> >> kernel /vmlinuz-2.6.12-gentoo-r4 root=/dev/hda5 ro lang=en vga=791
> >> boot
> >>
> >> This is straight out of my menu.lst file (the debian and
> gentoo name for
> >> grub.conf).  The grub.conf file's entries get executed as-is when you
> >> choose one at bootup time, as if you typed them yourself at the prompt.
> >> As you can see, my root filesystem is on /dev/hda5, the first extended
> >> partition of the disk.  You alluded to a syntax that lets grub figure
> >> out the root filesystem partition for itself (root=LABEL=/).  I suggest
> >> spelling it out explicitly as I have done here.
> >>
> >> Do you need an initrd image?  If it's a stock redhat kernel, I
> would say
> >> it's a certainty.  I have not used an initrd image for a long
> time, so I
> >> have no known working example to offer you.  But it's not too hard; it
> >> looks like the "kernel" line, except with no params.  Here's a googled
> >> one:
> >>
> >> initrd /initrd-2.4.18-0.12.img
> >>
> >> You would put this somewhere between the "root" line and the
> "boot" line.
> >> Again, you can see that "/boot" is not part of the path.  This is
> >> because /boot is its own partition on this machine.  If /boot were part
> >> of the root filesystem, all the paths in grub.conf would have "/boot"
> >> prepended.
> >>
> >> With a stock redhat kernel, your kernel will be unable to read
> your hard
> >> drive without the assistance of the modules in that initrd image.  I'd
> >> bet that is your problem.  No ATA support, no workie.  Add an initrd
> >> line to your grub commands in grub.conf, or type the lines in manually
> >> from the grub prompt.
> >>
> >> Carlos
> >>

On Sat, Aug 13, 2005 at 12:08:58PM -0700, John Jordan wrote:
> But having said that, sometimes I might not want to rip the whole 
> CD as one file. Lots of times the publisher will put several works on 
> one CD. For example, I am currently ripping a CD that has 
> Beethoven's 1st, 7th and Leonore #3 -- nine tracks. If I rip this as 
> three files, it will work even better than the stereo, because each 
> file will be one complete work.

Like Jeme, I don't think it's the best approach, but mp3splt and
mp3wrap are what you're looking for.  You can bundle multiple MP3s
into one playable file with mp3wrap, and if you change your mind,
split them back apart with mp3splt, all without re-encoding or
suchlike.

> Quotes use fewer keystrokes and are less likely to cause weird errors

It's not that big a deal. I've been ripping/encoding my collection in 
order. There were 12 CDs for Beethoven. So once I named a file 
Beethoven - Symphony #1.mp3, the next symphony will be #2, so I 
just up-arrow and change the 1 to a 2. I've been doing it for several 
hours today and haven't made an error yet. And if I do, I can always 
rename the file in Nautilus.

Note that I'm doing all the ID3 tag editing in gtkpod, which is 
copy/paste capable. Many of my CDs are by the same conductor 
and orchestra, so I can just paste them in. And gtkpod has no 
problem with spaces -- that problem was only in lame.

As for giving back to CDDB, the tags I want may not be what 
everyone else wants. For example, the Beethoven 9th by Bernstein 
in Berlin that I mentioned earlier today, is labeled in CDDB as 
album Ode to Freedom, artist Bernstein in Berlin, title Symphony 
No. 9. I didn't want Ode to Freedom to be the album name because 
that's actually the title of the fourth movement. And I am 
standardizing by using # instead of No. for the symphony number. 
You'll just have to color me weird, but it's my iPod and I want the 
tags to be what I want them to be, not what the fine folks at 
Deutsche Grammophon decided I'd want. At the same time, I doubt 
anyone would want me overwriting the database with my ideas of 
how the tags should read. So I'll just do it my way.

On Sat, 13 Aug 2005, John Jordan wrote:
> Note that I'm doing all the ID3 tag editing in gtkpod, which is 
> copy/paste capable. Many of my CDs are by the same conductor and 
> orchestra, so I can just paste them in.

this is a collosal waste of time.

Given your naming convention, you can do this all at once from the command 
line.

id3v2 -a "Ludwig van Beethoven" ./Beethoven*mp3

So all your artist fields are done.

If you're really into having filenames match ID3 tags, then you can just 
write a little script that parses the filename and fills in the tags.  I 
do that all the time with files I've downloaded that have informative 
filenames, but no ID3 tags.

This will save you HOURS of time.  I ripped two-hundred discs each day 
when I first bought my iPod.  Over that one long weekend (of thankfully 
miserable weather), I got the entire collection stored away and properly 
cataloged.

Type as little as possible.  Your wrists will thank you.  And mousing is 
even worse than typing.

> And I am standardizing by using # instead of No. for the symphony 
> number.

That's fine for the ID3 tags, but I'd recommend against using that for the 
filenames -- just one more thing you have to escape as the octothorp (#) 
is the sign you use to tell the shell to stop reading that line (good for 
adding comments and stuff).

> You'll just have to color me weird, but it's my iPod and I want the tags 
> to be what I want them to be, not what the fine folks at Deutsche 
> Grammophon decided I'd want.

Of course.  There are issues like that all over my collection.  But when 
there are spelling errors or the like, I think we all owe it to freedb to 
submit corrections.

> At the same time, I doubt anyone would want me overwriting the database 
> with my ideas of how the tags should read. So I'll just do it my way.

It's not an automated process.

>> You're doing this via USB?  Weird.  Is it USB 2.0?  I use firewire.
>
> My iPod came with a USB cable. A firewire cable is an optional item I'd 
> have to buy from Apple.

Ah.  I bought my iPod in March when they still had them in stock from 
before the "price reduction" (wherein they dropped the retail price fifty 
bucks and took eighty dollars worth of accessories out of the box).

Hence, mine came with a dock, two cables, and a power adapter.

> And yes, it is 2.0. Apple literature says it requires 2.0. But when 
> reformatting it to FAT32 I plugged it into a 1.1 port on my Windows 2000 
> desktop and it worked just fine.

Yeah, any USB will do.  It's just unpleasantly slow transfering files on 
old USB.  I've done it, too.

>>> Eventually I shut down and restarted the computer. That did it.
>>
>> You need the rescan-scsi-bus.sh script.
>>
>> When it gets flakey, you have to rescan the bus and verify the devices.

Jim,

In rescue mode, the distribution is mount on /sysimage/.  So your
grub.conf file is located at /sysimage/boot/grub/grub.conf.

There should have been a message about using chroot to move to
the /sysimage file system.  

The fstab file would be located in /sysimage/etc/fstab.

But, if you chroot /sysimage, then everything is located in their
"proper" places.

Ken
CAD2CAM.COM

I've been ripping and encoding while I do other things for the past 
couple days. Today I had occasion to use mp3wrap for the first 
time. The problem was that the idiots who made the CDs (a 2-CD 
set) put the first three tracks of a piece on CD-1 and the final track 
of the piece on CD-2. Kinda lame, huh?

On 8/15/05, Jim Webb <jimwebb at charter.net> wrote:
> Here's my /etc/fstab.
[snip]
> /dev/hde7           swap                    swap    defaults        0 0

If your swap partition is hda7 (as you mentioned in your email
earlier) then you need to change this line in /etc/fstab to reflect
that (instead of hd*E*7).

Hope that helps,
Jason

From jeme at brelin.net  Mon Aug 15 16:29:16 2005
From: jeme at brelin.net (Jeme A Brelin)

Subject: [PLUG] ipods
In-Reply-To: <43006A39.11426.37683837@localhost>

	<43006A39.11426.37683837@localhost>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0508151619510.31915@shaft.bitmine.net>


On Mon, 15 Aug 2005, John Jordan wrote:
> But when I tried to place it into the file list in gtkpod it appeared 
> that nothing happened. I tried it a second time and this time got an 
> error that the file was already listed in gtkpod. So I scrolled through 
> and found the file. It seems that gtkpod had taken the filename as 
> http://mp3split.sourceforge.net, believe it or not.
>
> Thinking I could fool gtkpod, I deleted it from the list in gtkpod, then 
> changed the filename on my computer to Serenade.mp3, deleting the 
> MP3WRAP. But no luck. Evidently gtkpod is smarter than me, as it still 
> took the filename as the URL. I guess it must look inside the file 
> somehow before adding it to the list of files to sync to the iPod.

OK, you clearly don't understand the concept of an ID3 tag and that could 
be why you're confused about this whole thing.

Part of the MP3 file format is a block of data where "metadata" (or 
"information about the information") is stored.  This metadata has a 
particular format that allows you to embed titles, artists, track names, 
and much more into the data itself.  So it doesn't matter what you NAME 
the file in your filesystem, the file "knows" its "real name".

gtkpod and most other MP3 playing applications read this metadata and 
ignore the filename you've assigned.

One of the fields in this metadata tag is "Track".  This is used to preset 
the order in which the MP3s that share the same "Album" field are ordered 
and played in most MP3 playing systems.  (XMMS doesn't do this by default, 
oddly, but its the only player I use that doesn't.  If anybody knows how 
to make it do it, please share.  Annoying as hell.)

> I also tried just copying the tracks onto my hard disk and then ripping 
> them all as one file, but the directories on the CDs are screwed up. I 
> get fragments of the filenames in what appears to be several files.
>
> I guess it was not my destiny to have this piece on my iPod. :(

Did you try ripping them as raw PCM audio and then joining those tracks 
and encoding them as a single MP3?  That was my first suggestion to you 
when you insisted on having one big file.  It will most certainly work, 
though you might have to manually insert the desired amount of space 
between tracks if the tracks end abruptly and are not padded.

> And no, I do not want to rip/encode as single tracks and then list them 
> under Album. I've tried that and I don't care for the results.

Exactly what about "the result" do you not "care for"?

More to the point, what behavior do you get that you don't want?  What 
behavior do you want that you don 't get?

I'm SUPER curious about the above, becuase my iPod plays multiple 
symphonic tracks EXACTLY like my CD player plays them and I can't imagine 
being happy with one and not the other.

> But if anyone has any other suggestions besides Mp3wrap, I'd like to 
> hear them.

I've already suggested ripping the audio and concatenating those files, 
then encoding and tagging them.  You lose the titles of the movements and 
the ability to easily navigate through them, but you get one big file of 
the whole piece.

J.

> tracks and encoding them as a single MP3?  That was my first

cdparanoia by default rips to a single file. You have to explicitly
pass it the "batch" option to get a separate file for each track. No
post-rip concatenation required.

I believe my sound card is /dev/audio.

Can someone suggest some tips on how I can debug why my sound
card stops recording input?  I have also checked and nothing is on MUTE.

thanks for any tips.

From ckonstan at lunarlogic.com  Tue Aug 16 09:54:16 2005
From: ckonstan at lunarlogic.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Tue, 16 Aug 2005 09:54:16 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Sound card won't record
In-Reply-To: <BAY108-F252A232D2F2950BCDE60A8B8B00@phx.gbl>
References: <BAY108-F252A232D2F2950BCDE60A8B8B00@phx.gbl>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0508160937300.6308@localhost>

Just a shot in the dark here: Is it possible that some other app is
holding the /dev/audio device open?  I believe (though I'm no expert in
this field) that the sound card can be used by only one app at a time.
When you fiddled with the loudness, you must have used some app to do
so.  Is it still running?

Maybe set up fluxbox or GnuStep as a debugging environment, which
doesn't have all the panel applets and stuff, and will therefore be
less likely to interfere with everything you're trying to do.  Or use 
TWM.

Permissions on the /dev/audio device?  When I first switched from debian
to gentoo, I went through the whole song and dance.  In gentoo, you must
be a member of the audio group to use the sound devices.  I don't
suppose this is your problem, as you made no mention that you just
switched distros.  Still, who knows if some recent package upgrade made
a policy change like this on your machine.

Often, the "device" which your apps point to is actually just a symlink
to a real device.  /dev/audio could easily be a symlink to /dev/audio1,
for example. Is the symlink still present?

Sounds like you're using a fairly sophisticated app to test your sound
card.  Why not remove some variables from the equation by attempting to
record with a more straightforward app?  Use "wavrec" to record sound to
a raw wav file.  It may be called "rec" on some distros.  May need to
get a microphone.  If that works but MythTV doesn't, at least you know
it's not your hardware.

Carlos

transactions are cleared.  I have a column where I put a symbol to
indicate that a transaction is clear.  Is there a way to get around
having to, by hand, make sure that the bank balance matches the 
spreadsheet balance?  Basically, I've copied the standard Washington
Mutual checkbook register with an added two columns that are for
a date and a bank balance ( I ignored the fee column ).  

I'm thinking I need to have the spreadsheet use a program as a formula.
A simple program that can take the necessary columns as say lists and
process them together.  The program must produce a balance to compare
to the bank's and the balance column.  For the balance column I'm
looking at:

     last_row_balance + current_row_deposit - current_row_payment

                                 .
                                 .
                                 .

For comparing to the bank balance I need to do:

     Balance + Deposit - Payment 

with one important gotcha.  Transactions that are not cleared should 
not be included in the calculation.  This is a dual input formula,
yes/no on a row's information and a running sum of what's being
added or subtracted.

One option instead of a flag column is a column where you enter each
transaction as it clears (requires the use of negative numbers) to
do a simple sum on.  I want this to be easy to understand
though and I don't like increasing the amount of typing that has
to be done.  Every time information has to be added to the spreadsheet,
there is greater potential for errors to be introduced.  Accuracy is
very important when you're trying to keep track of a checkbook.

-------------------------------------------------
This mail sent through IMP: http://horde.org/imp/


From scratchcomputing at gmail.com  Tue Aug 16 12:18:40 2005
From: scratchcomputing at gmail.com (Eric Wilhelm)
Date: Tue, 16 Aug 2005 12:18:40 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Openoffice special formula...
In-Reply-To: <1124208303.43020eaf28b43@xerxes.robinson-west.com>
References: <1124208303.43020eaf28b43@xerxes.robinson-west.com>
Message-ID: <200508161218.40733.ewilhelm@cpan.org>

# from plug_0 at robinson-west.com
# on Tuesday 16 August 2005 09:05 am:

>with one important gotcha. ?Transactions that are not cleared should
>not be included in the calculation. ?This is a dual input formula,
>yes/no on a row's information and a running sum of what's being
>added or subtracted.

OpenOffice has support for string comparison functions and conditional 
statements.  It's not pretty and you need to read the manual, but you 
can essentially do something like:

   $balance += (($cleared eq "*") ? $transaction : 0);

I know.  Perl makes it look so easy!  The formula's code *will* be 
uglier.

--Eric

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Tue Aug 16 21:50:07 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Tue, 16 Aug 2005 21:50:07 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] data array from a black and white graphics image
Message-ID: <20050817045007.GA1627@gate.kl-ic.com>


Is there any easy-to-use graphics software library with simple
routines that can be pointed at a two-level black-and-white
png/jpg/gif/tif/other? bitmap image, then returns an array of
ones and zeros?  C, C++, or Perl would be acceptable.  

Why?  I am doing a chip design and need to compute the resistance
of a rectangle with a random assortment of odd-shaped holes ( the
electrical equivalent of swiss cheese) with perhaps 10% accuracy.
The source data is unreadable ("GDS format" complex polygons), but
I have a rendering engine that runs under windoze that can draw a
reasonably accurate screen-sized black-and-white image, which I can
then capture with a screen dump.  After transforming the image to
the desired data array, I can throw it at a simple Poisson solver
and let it crank.  A CAD tool that did the whole shebang would be
nice, but I can probably write a simple one-off solver faster than
I could learn to use the tool.

So again, what library can do the image-to-array readin/transform
easily, which routines, and where can I find simple sample code?  
Alternately, which flat, uncompressed image formats are dead
simple to slurp?  I figure some folks here have actual experience
in this.

Keith

-- 
Keith Lofstrom          keithl at keithl.com         Voice (503)-520-1993
KLIC --- Keith Lofstrom Integrated Circuits --- "Your Ideas in Silicon"
Design Contracting in Bipolar and CMOS - Analog, Digital, and Scan ICs


From Jkarlock at earthlink.net  Tue Aug 16 22:57:35 2005

Subject: [PLUG] data array from a black and white graphics image
In-Reply-To: <20050817045007.GA1627@gate.kl-ic.com>

I dealt with this a few years ago to trace a faxed PCB into my cad. There 
is a type of tiff that is already just ones and zeros. Look at a B&W, 
uncompressed tiff, that is probably it. You just have to get the row width 
right.

Thanks
JK

From seniorr at aracnet.com  Wed Aug 17 01:56:57 2005
From: seniorr at aracnet.com (Russell Senior)
Date: 17 Aug 2005 01:56:57 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] data array from a black and white graphics image
In-Reply-To: <20050817045007.GA1627@gate.kl-ic.com>
References: <20050817045007.GA1627@gate.kl-ic.com>
Message-ID: <863bp90wme.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>

>>>>> "Keith" == Keith Lofstrom <keithl at kl-ic.com> writes:

Keith> Is there any easy-to-use graphics software library with simple
Keith> routines that can be pointed at a two-level black-and-white
Keith> png/jpg/gif/tif/other? bitmap image, then returns an array of
Keith> ones and zeros?  C, C++, or Perl would be acceptable.

As I learned about a year ago (Sept 2004) on this very mailing list:

  $ convert foo.png foo.txt 

will give you something that looks like:

  $ head foo.txt
  # ImageMagick pixel enumeration: 72,77,255,RGB
  0,0: (254,254,254) #FEFEFE
  1,0: (254,254,254) #FEFEFE
  2,0: (254,254,254) #FEFEFE
  3,0: (254,254,254) #FEFEFE
  4,0: (254,254,254) #FEFEFE
  5,0: (254,254,254) #FEFEFE
  6,0: (254,254,254) #FEFEFE
  7,0: (254,254,254) #FEFEFE
  8,0: (254,254,254) #FEFEFE

You ought to be able to hack that into whatever format you like pretty
easily.

From jeme at brelin.net  Wed Aug 17 02:36:13 2005
From: jeme at brelin.net (Jeme A Brelin)
Date: Wed, 17 Aug 2005 02:36:13 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Mp3 to WAV converter, EZ to use & install?
In-Reply-To: <200508162227.27321.guy1656@ados.com>
References: <200508162227.27321.guy1656@ados.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.61.0508170231060.31915@shaft.bitmine.net>


On Tue, 16 Aug 2005, GLL wrote:
> Does anybody know of a MP3 to WAV converter?
>
> I am running Mandrake 10 now.

Every MP3 player has at its heart an MP32WAV utility.  It's just a matter 
of letting the user close to it.

Odds are pretty good that your system has mpg123 (or its sister mpg321) 
installed already.

>From the man page mpg123(1):

   -w file, --wav
       Write output as WAV file. This will cause the MPEG stream to be
       decoded and saved as file file , or standard output if - is used
       as file name. You can also use --au and --cdr  for AU and CDR
       format, respectively.


if you've got a whole directory full of MP3 files that you'd like to make 
into WAV files (and they're currently named whatever.mp3 and you're happy 
with files correspondingly named whatever.wav), you can just do this:

for file in *mp3; do mpg123 -w `basename "$file" mp3`wav "$file"; done

Fancy.

J.
--

      Jeme A Brelin
     jeme at brelin.net

  http://www.openlaw.org

From: romanmir_ug at comcast.net (Chris Penwell)
Date: Wed, 17 Aug 2005 18:08:00 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Dual Boot - Two Drives
In-Reply-To: <430385AC.4050401@comcast.net>
References: <430385AC.4050401@comcast.net>
Message-ID: <4303DF70.5030705@comcast.net>

Richard C. Steffens wrote:

> I'm about to try dual booting with separate drives for Win98SE and 
> SuSE 9.3. I've got SuSE loaded and working on the first drive. I'm 
> about to disconnect that drive and install Win98SE on the other drive, 
> so it can't try to do anything to the Linux drive. Once finished, I 
> want to be able to boot, through Grub, to either OS.
>
> Has anyone done this, and have any "gotcha's" to share?
>
> I assume there are some directions for how to configure Grub and will 
> go read those.
>
> Any recommendations on which drive should be the slave and which the 
> master on the IDE controller?
>
> Thanks for any advice.
>
    I have had overwhelming success with having a pre-existing windows 
XP install on one drive, and Linux (used to be Mandrake, now Kubuntu) on 
a completely separate drive.

    As I mentioned, I had the windows install pre-existing. When I 
installed Mandrake, it auto-detected the windows install and created an 
entry for it (in lilo,) automagically. Kunbuntu not so much. Had to 
convert from grub to lilo, which for me was kinda scary. But lilo seems 
to work.

    I think that having the windows side of things pre-existing might 
make your life a little easier; though I don't know the ins and outs of 
a Suse install. Also which ever HDD is gonna have linux on it should 
probably be the primary/master. You might be able to tell your BIOS 
which HDD to boot first however.

    Just my $.02 worth of experience.

mysqlimport.exe databasename filename.sql

appreciated.

I don't know about the second problem, but for the first there's two
really good options I know of, you can use phpMyAdmin
(http://www.phpmyadmin.net/home_page/) for a good web interface to
MySQL, and you can use MySQL Control Center
(http://www.mysql.com/products/mysqlcc/) if you want a
locally-installed interface (which works on Windows).

If they are using Access, why not let them "link" to the MySQL database 
by building an ODBC connection to the MySQL database.  They can connect 
to the database using whatever permissions they've used in the past and 
view it the same way they would from Access.

If they're looking for a tool like "Access" on a client PC, REKALL 
(http://www.rekallrevealed.org/ or http://www.totalrekall.co.uk/) may be 
a valid option...

If that isn't acceptable....can you identify the client pieces and what 
you are trying to achieve?  Reporting from Windows is completely 
different than data-entry/analysis from Windows against a MySQL database 
(even though it shouldn't be!)

Tim

From ckonstan at lunarlogic.com  Thu Aug 18 19:19:57 2005
From: ckonstan at lunarlogic.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Thu, 18 Aug 2005 19:19:57 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Any lispers out there?  Newbie needs booster shot
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0508181745160.6330@localhost>

I am a software developer who has, up until now, used pay-dirt
languages exclusively (java, php, perl, other "hot" languages in
today's workaday world).

I have come to the realization that lisp is the only language that
matters.  I'm gobbling it up like a greedy child.  With any luck, I'll
find a way to use it at my paying job.

I have just written my first useful macro.  There is one small problem
with it that I do not have the lisp knowledge to solve.  I need to
know more about symbols vs. strings when used unquoted (preceded by
",") in a macro (or, really, in a backticked list).

Among other tasks, this macro writes a (defclass) and a (defmethod).
The name of the class I am creating is currently passed in as a symbol
(not a string).  Another argument of the macro is a URL (string).

I would like to be able to do away with the class name argument, since
the calling code does not need to know this bit of information.  I
would rather use the URL (a unique string) to derive a class name,
inside the macro definition.

Here's the relevant code (I'm using SBCL):

(defvar *document-root-url* nil
   "This is the public URL of the site.  Example: \"http://localhost:3000\".")
(setf *document-root-url*
       (let ((fqdn #+sbcl(sb-bsd-sockets:host-ent-name
                             (sb-bsd-sockets:get-host-by-name
                             (machine-instance)))
                   #-sbcl (format nil "localhost")))
         (make-url :scheme "http"
                   :host fqdn
                   :port *tcp-port*)))

(defvar *website-url* nil)
(setf *website-url*
       (urlstring
         (merge-url *document-root-url* "/jewelery")))

(defvar *title* "Pippi's Jewelery")

(defun make-absolute-url(url)
   "Prepends *WEBSITE-URL* to the given URL and returns the full URL as
a string."
   (concatenate 'string *website-url* url))

(defmacro publish-page (handler-class-name url &rest body)
   "Macro to do the grunt work of creating and installing a subclass of
HANDLER for each page you wish to publish.

Publishing a page entails 3 actions:
     - defining a class for the page that is a subclass of HANDLER;
     - implementing the handle-request-response method on this class;
     - installing an instance of the handler into the listener.

This macro automates the production of all this code."
   `(progn
      (defclass ,handler-class-name (handler) ())
      (defmethod handle-request-response ((handler ,handler-class-name)
                                           method
                                           request)
        (request-send-headers request)
        (html-stream (request-stream request) , at body))
      (install-handler (http-listener-handler *listener*)
                       (make-instance ',handler-class-name)
                       (make-absolute-url ,url)
                       t)))

(publish-page jewelery-home
               "/home"
               `(html
                 (head (title ,*title*))
                 (body ((h1 :align "center") "Hello Pip"))))


This is part of a simple website page publisher.  It uses araneida as
the web server API.  Please assume that functions like MERGE-URL and
URLSTRING are provided by the API and just work.  *document-root-url*,
by the way, is an object, not a string.  We want a string for the call
to INSTALL-HANDLER.  That part works - I'm worried about something
else in this code.

The code I didn't show you (because it works and has nothing to do
with the problem) supplies an instance of an araneida LISTENER class
in the constant *listener*.  *listener* has a slot to hold a single
DISPATCHING-HANDLER object, which is the container for the collection
of HANDLER instances.  This alist of HANDLER objects is keyed by URL
string.

A HANDLER is nothing more than a class with no slots and a single
method, HANDLE-REQUEST-RESPONSE.  The URL is used at request time to
look up the corresponding subcless of HANDLER, and calling the
HANDLE-REQUEST-RESPONSE method specialized on that subclass gets us to
the right function to render the page.  That is all done by the
araneida API.  To use the API, all we need to do is populate
DISPATCHING-HANDLER with HANDLER subclasses.

Another user-written lisp file is responsible for creating the
*listener* instance and putting the singeton root DISPATCHING-HANDLER
in it.  The code supplied above is what adds the HANDLER instances to
the DISPATCHING-HANDLER using INSTALL-HANDLER.

PUBLISH-PAGE is the macro that automates the writing of the code for
creating and installing a page handler.  It creates a subclass of
HANDLER.  Then it overrides the HANDLE-REQUEST-RESPONSE method, which
will get called by araneida when a request to the matching URL is
made.  Then it calls INSTALL-HANDLER to place the sublassed HANDLER
into the DISPATCHING-HANDLER.  This macro is where I need help.

There are 2 places where I run up against my limited lisp knowledge.
Both involve the class name:

      (defclass ,handler-class-name (handler) ())
      (defmethod handle-request-response ((handler ,handler-class-name)
                                           method
                                           request)

I shouldn't be passing in handler-class-name, since the code outside
this macro has no reason to care about the name of the class.  I
should be generating the class name somehow.  I can use the URL string
for this.  If my goal were to simply make another string that is based
off the URL, that would be easy.  I'm sure it will be the first step
of any solution to my problem.

Ultimately, I need the class name to be a symbol though, not a string.
The places where I put ",handler-class-name" need to be symbols.  That
is why it looks like this when I call the macro:

     (publish-page jewelery-home
                   "/home"
                   `(html
                     (head (title ,*title*))
                     (body ((h1 :align "center") "Hello Pip"))))

jewelery-home is not quoted or stringified.  It must be through some
magic of DEFMACRO argument lists that I am able to use this uninterned
symbol with no value in this way withoug a compiler error.

Is there a way to turn a string into a symbol, or get a symbol
representation of a string?  If so, I could quote jewelery-home and
treat it like a string.  Or better yet, I could transform the URL into
a class name using string handling functions.

I looked at INTERN and FIND-SYMBOL as a way of converting a string to
a symbol and back again.  I'm guessing, however, that there is a
common idiom for what I am trying to do, and I just need it to be
brought to my attention.

The question again, stated clearly this time:

In lisp, how do you convert a string into a symbol and place it,
unquoted, in a quoted list (as in a macro body)?

Carlos

Yes indeed, I have used MACROEXPAND-1 to see the fruits of my labors.
That is how I came to realize that I cannot pass in handler-class-name
as a string, because it gets written into the macro output with
quotes.  Maybe I could use PRINC to strip the quotes, but that seems
hacky.  I really want to use the right method, and do it the Lisp Way.
To me, that means avoiding string representations of code whenever
possible.  I do need to deal with handler-class-name as a string when
I'm producing it, but I want it to be a symbol when I apply it to the
DEFCLASS and DEFMETHOD forms.

I may try INTERN.  It looks promising.

Carlos

From seniorr at aracnet.com  Fri Aug 19 18:58:44 2005
From: seniorr at aracnet.com (Russell Senior)
Date: 19 Aug 2005 18:58:44 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] Any lispers out there?  Newbie needs booster shot
In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0508181745160.6330@localhost>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0508181745160.6330@localhost>
Message-ID: <868xyxtlm3.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>

>>>>> "Carlos" == Carlos Konstanski <ckonstan at lunarlogic.com> writes:

Carlos> I shouldn't be passing in handler-class-name, since the code
Carlos> outside this macro has no reason to care about the name of the
Carlos> class.  I should be generating the class name somehow.

Is this useful?

  * (describe 'gensym)

  GENSYM is an external symbol in #<PACKAGE "COMMON-LISP">.
  Function: #<FUNCTION GENSYM>
  Its associated name (as in FUNCTION-LAMBDA-EXPRESSION) is GENSYM.
  The function's arguments are:  (&OPTIONAL (THING G))
  Function documentation:
    Creates a new uninterned symbol whose name is a prefix string (defaults
     to "G"), followed by a decimal number. Thing, when supplied, will
     alter the prefix if it is a string, or be used for the decimal number
     if it is a number, of this symbol. The default value of the number is
     the current value of *gensym-counter* which is incremented each time
     it is used.
  Its declared argument types are:
    (&OPTIONAL (OR (VECTOR CHARACTER) (VECTOR NIL) BASE-STRING UNSIGNED-BYTE))
  Its result type is:
    (VALUES SYMBOL &OPTIONAL)

From ckonstan at lunarlogic.com  Fri Aug 19 21:42:53 2005
From: ckonstan at lunarlogic.com (Carlos Konstanski)
Date: Fri, 19 Aug 2005 21:42:53 -0700 (PDT)
Subject: [PLUG] Any lispers out there?  Newbie needs booster shot
In-Reply-To: <868xyxtlm3.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
References: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0508181745160.6330@localhost>
	<868xyxtlm3.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.63.0508192137020.6391@localhost>

GENSYM worked for me this time.  I tried it at some earlier point, and
I got a compiler error - it said the symbol was not a valid class
name.  The macro was in poor shape then - it was a symptom of another
problem.

This solution is very lispy, and I thank you.  Short, sweet, no
strings, no need to convert the URL to a class name even.  Just a LET:


(defmacro publish-page (url &rest body)
   (let ((handler-class-name (gensym)))
     `(progn
        (defclass ,handler-class-name (handler) ())
        (defmethod handle-request-response ((handler ,handler-class-name) method request)
          (request-send-headers request)
          (html-stream (request-stream request) , at body))
        (install-handler (http-listener-handler *listener*)
                         (make-instance ',handler-class-name)
                         (make-absolute-url ,url)
                         t))))


Lisp rocks.

Carlos

>  * (describe 'gensym)
>
>  GENSYM is an external symbol in #<PACKAGE "COMMON-LISP">.
>  Function: #<FUNCTION GENSYM>
>  Its associated name (as in FUNCTION-LAMBDA-EXPRESSION) is GENSYM.
>  The function's arguments are:  (&OPTIONAL (THING G))
>  Function documentation:
>    Creates a new uninterned symbol whose name is a prefix string (defaults
>     to "G"), followed by a decimal number. Thing, when supplied, will
>     alter the prefix if it is a string, or be used for the decimal number
>     if it is a number, of this symbol. The default value of the number is
>     the current value of *gensym-counter* which is incremented each time
>     it is used.
>  Its declared argument types are:
>    (&OPTIONAL (OR (VECTOR CHARACTER) (VECTOR NIL) BASE-STRING UNSIGNED-BYTE))
>  Its result type is:
>    (VALUES SYMBOL &OPTIONAL)

>On Tue, 16 Aug 2005, GLL wrote:
>>Does anybody know of a MP3 to WAV converter?
>>
>>I am running Mandrake 10 now.
>
>Every MP3 player has at its heart an MP32WAV utility.  It's just a matter 
>of letting the user close to it.
>
>Odds are pretty good that your system has mpg123 (or its sister mpg321) 
>installed already.
>
>>From the man page mpg123(1):
>
>   -w file, --wav
>       Write output as WAV file. This will cause the MPEG stream to be
>       decoded and saved as file file , or standard output if - is used
>       as file name. You can also use --au and --cdr  for AU and CDR
>       format, respectively.
>
>
>if you've got a whole directory full of MP3 files that you'd like to make 
>into WAV files (and they're currently named whatever.mp3 and you're happy 
>with files correspondingly named whatever.wav), you can just do this:
>
>for file in *mp3; do mpg123 -w `basename "$file" mp3`wav "$file"; done
>
>Fancy.

From keithl at kl-ic.com  Fri Aug 19 22:37:30 2005
From: keithl at kl-ic.com (Keith Lofstrom)
Date: Fri, 19 Aug 2005 22:37:30 -0700
Subject: [PLUG] data array from a black and white graphics image (solved)
In-Reply-To: <863bp90wme.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
References: <20050817045007.GA1627@gate.kl-ic.com>
	<863bp90wme.fsf@coulee.tdb.com>
Message-ID: <20050820053730.GA23618@gate.kl-ic.com>

>>>>> "Keith" == Keith Lofstrom <keithl at kl-ic.com> writes:

Keith> Is there any easy-to-use graphics software library with simple
Keith> routines that can be pointed at a two-level black-and-white
Keith> png/jpg/gif/tif/other? bitmap image, then returns an array of
Keith> ones and zeros?  C, C++, or Perl would be acceptable.
 
On Wed, Aug 17, 2005 at 01:56:57AM -0700, Russell Senior wrote:
> As I learned about a year ago (Sept 2004) on this very mailing list:
> 
>   $ convert foo.png foo.txt 
> 
> will give you something that looks like:
> 
>   $ head foo.txt
>   # ImageMagick pixel enumeration: 72,77,255,RGB
>   0,0: (254,254,254) #FEFEFE
>   1,0: (254,254,254) #FEFEFE
>   2,0: (254,254,254) #FEFEFE
>   3,0: (254,254,254) #FEFEFE
>   4,0: (254,254,254) #FEFEFE
> 
...


That got me started.  The way I ended up going, though, was to use
the text ("P2") form of the .pgm (portable gray map) format.  This
is a simple header, followed by a list of single decimal values for
each grayscale pixel.  I now have a simple program with fixed array
sizes, and I will tweak a bit more on it to use libslack to call
malloc so I can use variable-sized arrays.  

What I wrote is very slow, a simple diffusion-with-acceleration 
Poisson solution, but I let it crank overnight and it makes dandy-
looking field plots (also in pgm).  I didn't have a good way to
make contour lines through the data, so I did "zebra plots" AKA
band contours, where zones of similar value get the same gray level
in alternating bands.  Easy to code, just scale the value of the
pixels by the number of desired bands, truncate to integers, then
AND-out the LSB, scaling the result back to one of the two gray
levels.  Looks like zebra stripes.

In general, I am quite pleased with the results, and entering the
geometry for the shapes I need to study is quite easy using screen
captures from my CAD tools, with some touch-up in gimp.  I think I
shall put the program up on the web and see who can develop it into
a more general tool, or speed up the calculations. 

Keith

I have to speak up here.

LISP was a language we used in college, mostly for proof-of-concept.  
The neat thing about LISP is that you can "black box" everything.  If 
you need a routine but don't know how to do that routine, you flowchart 
it as a black box, and then see about getting it to run or better yet 
get someone else to build it.

Eventually we discovered that LISP is more of a theoretical language.  
Its compiled binaries are slow and clunky.

We determined that LISP stood for "Lots of Interesting Silly Parentheses."

If you're using JAVA, php, perl, C(+...), etc., STICK WITH THEM.  They 
will make you money.  LISP is more of an academic language for theories 
and such.

RP

I have to speak up here. Yes, Lisp is indeed a theoretical language. 
However, its compiled binaries aren't necessarily slow and clunky any 
more. GCL, CMUCL and SBCL, all free and open source, by the way, are 
quite efficient, and if you want an even more efficient way, there's Scheme.

There are two application areas where Lisp still reigns supreme. One is 
symbolic mathematics -- Maxima is the best known free package. The other 
is "artificial intelligence".
